<user_name>Cynthia Guiang</user_name><Date>1605978032854<//Date><rate>5<//rate>< Text>
I have forever fostered two dogs with this organization so far. They were very supportive and truly care for each and every animal that comes into their care. I've read some negative reviews. One thing I will say, they are very selective about who fosters and adopts. These animals have been through a lot. They are vulnerable and many have health issues due to their age and/or previous treatment. The last thing FFF wants is to put these animals in the wrong home...again. Some may take this scrutiny personally, but I understand how necessary it is. FFF is there to advocate for the animal, not to try and "sell" you...so while the animals get the red carpet (they literally drive hundreds of miles and spend thousands of dollars to rescue these seniors), they may not roll it out for you. It's not personal, you are not the priority. And please keep in mind that most of the people you are interacting with are volunteering! If you care about their mission, then you will understand and share in their priorities (and give them a little leeway on human customer service). The FFF community is amazing...and the loving homes that these animals find for their final days is so heartwarming. I'm so glad FFF exists and would vouch for their integrity 100%.< /Text>

<Review>I had a previous bad experience with this rescue but put it aside because I understand we all have bad days and that I was adopting a dog and not the rescue. Other than adopting two amazing dogs, my second experience with them was even worse.

First, I adopted my dogs outright. That means I am responsible for all their costs. However, on the FF Facebook page their adoption announcement was accompanied by a request for monthly ‚Äúsponsorship‚Äù. Since I‚Äôm responsible for their costs this confused me so I asked. I was told that this money would go to a general fund and not for these two dogs in particular. I pointed out that this was misleading and was told ‚ÄúAnyone who signs up as a fan is able to get more information from our website about the program and what being a fan entails.‚Äù So you need to go to another site and read the fine print to know that you are not actually supporting the dogs your ‚Äúsponsoring ‚Äú, which people clearly aren't doing based on the comments to the post.

I was also told that they "don't include that information in every social media post just because it would likely start to be redundant".  Putting aside that I would rather be redundant than misleading, I proposed to them that they simply change the language from a request for sponsorship to one asking for to help recover the costs spent for the dogs, to help with potential medical emergencies, and to help other senior dogs in need.  No response.

The adoption contract has clauses in it that muddy the ownership status of the adopter. For example, it requires that microchips  be registered with FF as the primary contact. Microchip registration serves as proof of ownership since dogs are viewed as property under the law. Also,  if something happens to my dogs I need to wait for FF to contact me because my dogs microchip only allow one contact.

I‚Äôve fostered for many other rescues and generally dogs will get a dental before they‚Äôre adopted. FF did not and would not contribute to the cost,  so the cost of it fell entirely to me while FF is soliciting ‚Äúsponsorship ‚Äú for them.  And frankly, putting senior dogs under anesthesia twice (they would eventually need dentals and were already scheduled for other surgeries) is not optimal.

Equally disingenuous was their statement in their adoption post indicating that it had been their intention to keep the dogs as a pair. That couldn‚Äôt be farther from the truth. I was interested in one and requested more information. Was not told about the other. When I requested more information I read that he had come in with another dog. I asked to meet them both. When I went to meet them both I as clearly told that they didn‚Äôt have to be adopted together. It was me, not FF, who insisted they stay together. FF does do amazing things, but they shouldn‚Äôt be  taking credit for something  they very much did not do.

As to their awareness of medical issues, one of my dogs came with a nasty case of worms despite having been at FF for some time. The other dog, who had been picked up as a stray with her, but who spent a longer time in a shelter, did not. Since they were found together they would have eaten there same things and been in the same places, so they should have both had worms. My guess is that the shelter did notice his worms and treated them before releasing him.

In addition, they were aware that I was moving out of SD but couldn‚Äôt get an appointment for the dogs mass removal until a week before. No one mentioned to me that her stitches would need to be removed a week to 10 days later, when I was in a new home and far from a vet I knew. Luckily I  had experience with mass removals, but what if I hadn‚Äôt? That‚Äôs putting the dogs in a precarious position.  Another way to put senior dogs in a precarious position is to set them up for needing to undergo anesthesia twice- they were already scheduled for surgery so it makes sense to do the dentals at the same time.

Overall, this has been an extremely disappointing experience. If you want to adopt a senior dog I strongly recommend Lionel‚Äôs Legacy.<//Review><pics>None<//pics><Resp>None</Resp><Gmap_id>0x80dbe8dc94db467d:0x206ccb2aa6c6615d< /Gmap_id></record>

< text>
I started volunteering at Frosted Faces last April. Right away I was impressed with how much the rescue coordinators and volunteers care about rescuing senior dogs and cats, and giving them their best life no matter how long it may be. Frosted Faces is an actual home that has been modified to be a safe, animal friendly facility. The kennels are cleaned multiple times daily, and there are 7 play yards for dogs to enjoy being outside.  Dogs are constantly walked, bathed, and are given so much love and attention. I look forward to volunteering my time there each week.

Three months ago I met Frosted Face Miller as a volunteer taking him to a vet appointment. I fell in love with him immediately. With two cocker spaniels at home we never thought we would adopt a bully breed! There was just a feeling that he needed us. As with all people looking to adopt, we went through a home inspection and brought our current dogs to Frosted Faces to see if all three dogs would get along. It was clear Miller was to be a part of our family!  Miller has thrived in our home. It has become apparent to us that we didn‚Äôt just choose Miller, he chose US to be his family!

If you are looking for a senior dog or cat, I highly recommend Frosted Faces! To be a volunteer there is a privilege and we will continue to adopt from them!  Thank you Kelly, Andy, Jenna, Alicia and all the volunteers who work together to make Frosted Faces such a wonderful organization!< /text>

{'time': 1578430227200, 'text': 'Hi Randy,\nThank you for visiting Frosted Faces Foundation with interest in adopting a senior dog! We do introduce guests who attend our Open Houses to all of the dogs on-site and volunteers answer questions to the best of their knowledge.\n\nIt is included in our very first email of correspondence with applicants, "*Please note that we are constantly screening applicants and cannot promise any specific animal will still be available, but we will do our best to find a great match for you!"\n\nIt also says on the Application website page, "*Frosted Faces will go home with the first approved and scheduled applicant."\n\nWe say these things because we are constantly screening applications and people do choose dogs for whom they did not apply during their scheduled introduction.\n\nThe screening process is clearly outlined in the first email from Adoption Coordinator once you apply, "I will be assigning a volunteer to schedule a home inspection with you to ensure a Frosted Face will be loved and safe in your home. A home inspection lasts 15-30 minutes, and the volunteer is instructed to complete an online form and take photos of your living indoor and outdoor space for review.\n\nThe home inspector is required to contact you within 12 hours of assignment, to have your home inspection completed within 3 days if your schedule permits, and they are to have submitted their report within 12 hours of their visit."\n\nOur screening process is also outlined on the Application page of our website, "Expect your application to be fully evaluated, along with contacting references, and completion of a home inspection within 3-5 days."  This process is also outlined on our Frequently Asked Questions page:\nWhat is the process to become a Family to a Frosted Face?\n1. Fill out the Application as completely and thoughtfully as possible.\n2. An application screener will email you to ask follow up questions, review your expectations, and schedule a home check.\n3. A volunteer from FFF will home check you to verify that your home is dog-friendly and prepared to take in a Frosted Face.\n4. Upon passing, your application screener will coordinate an appointment for you to visit Frosted Faces Foundation and choose a dog."\n\nWe do ask approved adopters to bring their current dogs to the appointment so that we can help with proper dog introductions to decrease liability and make sure it\'s a safe match.\n\nAdoption Coordinators let applicants know when the dog they were interested was adopted within 24 hours, although we do hope that applicants follow through with the screening process and choose another dog in need.\n\nWhile a senior dog finding permanent placement should be celebrated, we are sorry that this caused you disappointment because it was not in your home.  There are many dogs in need and we hope that you choose to rescue another.'}</Resp>

Update:
I received an email on 7-Jan 2020, after having written this review. It is almost an exact copy-and-paste of this response, but leaves out one thing, reproduced below: I was requested to remove my review. There was absolutely no interest in understanding why I wrote the review or why I felt I had a negative experience. The implication is simply that I did not understand FFF's protocols, and so was therefore disappointed with myself and should find a different way to handle it.

From Kelly Sm√≠≈°ek:
"I would like to ask you to consider removing your negative review about our organization.  Your reaction only negatively impacts the dogs in our care and there are more effective ways to handle your disappointment with misunderstanding our protocols."

I love dogs and only wanted to adopt a senior dog. I commend FFF and their staff for the work they do with helping these beautiful pups. I plan to continue to visit shelters and open our home and hearts to a dog in need. However, I will not work with somebody who cannot be bothered to take the time to understand why somebody felt a need to write a negative review about their own business, and simply assumes it is entirely because of our own misunderstanding.

Original Review:

We spent time with a Frosted Face for over an hour on a Saturday afternoon, and had a chance to speak with a Kennel Manager who had hosted her on a Frosted Fling for two weeks. She was able to provide a lot of useful information about the dog, including how she is in a car, what she eats, how she is with other dogs & people, etc. We were very positive about the experience. We discussed with the Kennel Manager that we didn't think we needed to bring in our existing dog to meet the Frosted Face, as it might not represent a natural setting for them. The Kennel Manager agreed. We applied to adopt her that night and were very much looking forward to having her in our family. The next day we just happen to notice on Instagram that she had been adopted. We were quite sad to see this. We received no notification at all. We also found out afterwards via email that there was more involved in the adoption process than what we had just discussed with the Kennel Manager the day before, including bringing our existing dog with us to FFF for a meeting with the Frosted Face we were interested in. While I am extremely thankful that a organization like Frosted Faces exists to take care of these beautiful senior dogs, I'm very disappointed with our first interaction with Frosted Faces Foundation.<//Review>

<user_name>Gladys J<//user_name><time>1480628668518< /time><rate>5<//rate>< Text>
Hands down the best place to throw a kid party!

Our 5-year-old loves open play at this place. So naturally we knew Imagine Me Grow would be the perfect place to throw our youngest daughter's 1st birthday party. And boy were we right! It was completely stress-free and there was no mess to clean up afterwards.

We were allowed to bring in our own food/decorations; however, you can also purchase them through Imagine Me Grow. But regardless, the staff, which by the way, were the sweetest, helped set up our party decor and food/dessert stations. Oh, and they even took photos as well!

Also, most kid party centers do not allow you to bring in your own food so this was a major plus for us as our oldest has a couple severe food allergies.

But the best part of it all was that all of our guests had an amazing time. Everyone kept complimenting how fun and cute the place was. Some even mentioned they'd like to throw their next kids birthday party there.<//Text>

<Rate>5<//Rate><Date>1527774835596<//Date><gmap_id>0x80db7de51c1838ab:0xc3aec1137bfd228<//gmap_id><user_name>travis knowlton<//user_name></record></dataset><record>
<user_id>117711686788524967812</user_id><user_name>Meri Willard</user_name>< date>
1457745779244</date>
< Rate>
5< /Rate>
<text>Wonderful fun play stations! We attended a birthday party here today for a classmate of my son. 4/5 year olds and their siblings were welcomed and allowed to play and explore. It reminded me of a  children's pottery barn catalog brought to life! Very sweet moments as my son and friends served one another in the bakery and sea food restaurant. My younger two loved the fire station very much. The cars can be pushed around the road and this was a please t surprise. The dance room was often empty but once in a while the children would enter and burst into dance. It was fun! Each room has a small screen tv with the rooms topic playing on the screen. At first I felt this was unecessary but as the party progressed it made sense, and had no sound so it wasn't intrusive to their imaginative play.

A music room would be fun, but trust me the kids were very satisfied and the play kitchens, fire station and dance room seemed to be my three boys favorite.

If I had to give any critique it would be to share that it is not a tactile/sensory experience as it is very clean and free of any sand or water play. That is understandable as it accomadates cooperative play amongst many children, young children. The environment fostered cooperative play and surprisingly allowed children the freedom to cooperate and play individually. I highly recommend!

In a time where children play centers resemble casinos and bars, and are often filled with video games this was refreshing!

Created for the younger child I find it sweet that they are not bombarded with flashing lights and bribery of candy and cheap toys. If my older kids were with me I could see them getting a little "bored" but I would encourage them to play and pretend with their younger siblings and I know the entire family would be better for it! So often we spend time and money to celebrate our children but we end up just consuming and teaching them greed and consuming. This truly fosters imaginative play that will help families bond, social skills flourish and develop life long memories.< /text><pics>None<//pics>< Resp>
None<//Resp>

< Text>
Accessible location with ample parking for all. They also have a lot of fitting room that you can use.

For a fewer crowd and shorter line, try to visit during early mornings (right after it opens) or late evenings (before it closes).

People here are friendly and kind to all. The greeter or theft prevention personnel is always cheerful and welcomes you warmly the moment you enter. I personally appreciate Johnny, he always give us product feedback whenever asked.

They have plenty of choices for clothing, toys & kitchen utensils. I also enjoy their choices for arts and crafts and home decorations.

Definitely our to-go-to whenever we want to shop!<//Text>

< review>
Large selection of men, women and children's clothes as well as purses/backpacks at decent prices. The home and shoe sections are small, as is the electronics section.
The store itself is packed tight and the aisles are rather small. During my visit today, I noticed a lack of maintenance throughout the store. The carts were mucky and the floors were dirty - and the changing rooms were untidy, with doors that wouldn't close.

In short - if you need a quick one-stop-shop for clothes/bags, the selection here is great. But if you're looking to enjoy the experience of browsing, this store may not be what you're looking for.</review>
